{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01Bs9BoteCWRjy2kJdnfnjRW","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"Now I see the pattern. The `video_vendor_dmi_table` in acer-wmi.c has several Acer models listed, and for each one, it calls `video_set_backlight_video_vendor` which disables the brightness capability in acer-wmi and lets the generic video driver handle it.\n\nThe Acer TravelMate 5735Z is not listed in this table! And based on the bug report, it should be using the native ACPI video backlight, not the vendor (acer_wmi) backlight.\n\nHowever, the issue might be more fundamental. Let me trace through the logic:\n\n1. When acer-wmi loads, it checks if the system is in video_vendor_dmi_table\n2. If yes, it calls video_set_backlight_video_vendor which disables acer-wmi brightness\n3. If the system is NOT in the table, acer-wmi will:\n   - Check what backlight type is selected via acpi_video_get_backlight_type()\n   - If it's not vendor, disable acer-wmi brightness (line 2210-2211)\n   - Otherwise, acer-wmi will register its own brightness interface\n\nThe problem for Acer TravelMate 5735Z is:\n- It's not in the video_vendor_dmi_table\n- By default (without kernel parameter), the backlight type is determined by acpi_video_get_backlight_type()\n- If that returns acpi_backlight_vendor, acer-wmi will register its interface (5 levels)\n- If that returns anything else, acer-wmi will disable its interface\n- The user can force it to work with acpi_backlight=native\n\nSo the fix could be:\n1. Add Acer TravelMate 5735Z to the DMI quirks table in video_detect.c with video_detect_force_native\n2. OR add it to the video_vendor_dmi_table in acer-wmi.c with the callback that disables acer-wmi brightness\n\n\nThe bug report shows that with `acpi_backlight=native`, the device gets 15-16 brightness levels, which indicates the native ACPI video driver is the correct choice. This means I should add an entry to video_detect.c's DMI table to force native backlight detection for this model, rather than modifying acer-wmi.c. The user's experience confirms that the vendor driver isn't providing adequate brightness control on this hardware. The logic in video_detect.c shows that without a DMI quirk entry, the function checks for ACPI_VIDEO_BACKLIGHT capability—if absent, it defaults to vendor. But since native works when explicitly set, the device must support it. The problem likely stems from the ACPI VIDEO backlight capability not being properly detected at boot, or the system being Win8 without BACKLIGHT_RAW registered. Looking at the actual backlight interfaces available, only intel_backlight appears by default, yet acer_wmi shows up when that driver is forced, and native mode successfully controls brightness through intel_backlight.\n\nThe fix would be adding this device to the DMI table to force native backlight selection. In acer-wmi.c, when a system matches video_vendor_dmi_table, it calls acpi_video_set_dmi_backlight_type(acpi_backlight_vendor) before checking the backlight type, and the callback also directly disables brightness capability if the type doesn't match vendor.\n\nSince the Acer TravelMate 5735Z isn't in this table, acer-wmi is likely registering its own backlight handler by default. The solution is either adding it to video_vendor_dmi_table in acer-wmi.c to disable acer-wmi brightness and let the generic video driver handle it, or adding it to video_detect_dmi_table in video_detect.c with force_native to use the native backlight driver instead.\n\nLooking at the check in acer-wmi around lines 2210-2211, if acpi_video_get_backlight_type() returns anything other than acpi_backlight_vendor, acer-wmi disables its brightness capability. The fact that the user is getting 5 brightness levels from acer_wmi suggests acpi_video_get_backlight_type() is returning acpi_backlight_vendor, which happens when there's no command-line override and no DMI quirk matching the system.\n\nSince the device works properly with acpi_backlight=native, the solution is to add a DMI entry to video_detect_dmi_table that forces native backlight handling for this specific device. I should verify whether video_vendor_dmi_table (which forces the generic video driver) would be more appropriate, but the key is understanding how acpi_video_get_backlight_type() determines which interface gets priority—vendor-specific drivers, the generic ACPI video driver, or native backlight control.\n\nThe acer-wmi driver checks this return value and disables its brightness capability if the type isn't set to vendor, which explains why the vendor driver fails here while the native driver succeeds. Adding the TravelMate 5735Z to the appropriate DMI table will ensure the native backlight driver is selected by default instead of relying on the broken vendor implementation.\n\nHowever, there's a complication: acer-wmi itself is calling acpi_video_set_dmi_backlight_type() to force vendor mode on certain systems. This means the driver is actively setting the backlight type through its own DMI table (video_vendor_dmi_table) before the brightness check happens. The sequence involves video_detect.c setting the initial type, then acer-wmi potentially overriding it based on its own hardware list.\n\nFor the TravelMate 5735Z specifically, neither video_detect.c nor acer-wmi.c has a matching entry, so the system defaults to vendor backlight handling. The user needs to decide whether to add the device to video_detect.c's table with force_native, or to acer-wmi.c's table to prevent the vendor override.\n\nSince native backlight works for this model, adding it to video_detect.c makes sense. However, there's a consideration about whether acer-wmi.c should also have an entry—potentially without a callback—to ensure it doesn't interfere with the video_detect decision. Looking at the existing code structure in acer-wmi.c around line 630, there are examples of entries that don't register their own backlight handler, relying instead on the acpi_video interface.\n\nThe most straightforward approach is adding the device to video_detect_dmi_table with force_native, which will prioritize the native intel_backlight driver. The core issue is that the backlight type defaults to vendor mode even though the native driver is available and functional on this hardware. intel_backlight works. The solution is to ensure intel_backlight gets used instead of acer_wmi by having acpi_video_get_backlight_type() return native for this device. Adding the Acer TravelMate 5735Z to video_detect_dmi_table with video_detect_force_native should resolve this.
